## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials science (thermomechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables map directly to a constitutive relation for a solid: stress (sigma) as a function of strain (epsilon) with temperature (T) affecting elastic modulus, yield/flow stress, and hardening/softening. Common models combine an elastic or hyperelastic stress–strain law with temperature-dependent material parameters and thermal strain offsets.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelasticity (Hooke + thermal strain): sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1 * T + c2) (small-strain stress with thermal expansion/offset)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear in T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic modulus softening/stiffening with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential softening): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (strong temperature sensitivity of stiffness)
- Nonlinear elastic (quadratic/cubic): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (finite-strain polynomial approximation)
- Ramberg–Osgood-type inverted form (power hardening): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * (c2 * epsilon)**c3 (elastic + nonlinear hardening contribution)
- Hollomon power-law (plastic flow proxy): sigma = c0 * (c1 * epsilon)**c2 (strain hardening dominated regime)
- Swift-type hardening: sigma = c0 * (c1 * epsilon + c2)**c3 (hardening with pre-strain/offset)
- Voce-type saturation hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * (c2 + exp(c3 * epsilon)) (stress approaches saturation with increasing strain)
- Hyperelastic (neo-Hookean-inspired 1D proxy): sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1) - c2 / (epsilon + c3) (captures stiffening at large deformation with asymmetry)
- Thermal softening multiplier on hardening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (flow stress reduced/increased by temperature via multiplicative factor)
- Polynomial thermal softening on hardening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T + c5 * T**2) (empirical temperature-dependent flow stress)
- Yield-like transition with smooth activation: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * log(c2 + exp(c3 * (epsilon - c4))) (smooth elastic-to-plastic transition without piecewise rules)
- Coupled cross-term expansion: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * T + c3 * epsilon * T + c4 * epsilon**2 * T (thermomechanical coupling via interaction terms)
- Log-strain sensitivity with temperature scaling: sigma = (c0 + c1 * log(c2 + epsilon)) * (c3 + c4 * T) (materials showing logarithmic hardening with T-dependent level)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic regime identification: sigma approximately proportional to epsilon at small epsilon suggests sigma ≈ E(T)*epsilon with E(T) slowly varying in T.
- Thermal expansion offset: if sigma at fixed epsilon shifts roughly linearly with T (including sign change), include (epsilon + c*T + c0) inside the stress law.
- Temperature softening of strength: monotonic decrease of sigma with increasing T at fixed epsilon is often captured by a multiplicative exp(c*T) (with c<0) or low-order polynomial in T multiplying a hardening term.
- Strain hardening signature: curvature upward in sigma vs epsilon (in log-log close to linear) suggests power-law forms (c*epsilon)^n or (c*epsilon+c0)^n.
- Saturation/plateau in sigma vs epsilon: diminishing slope at large epsilon indicates a saturating hardening structure (e.g., c0 + c1*(1 - exp(c*epsilon)) or equivalent rational/exponential forms).
- Elastic–plastic transition: a distinct knee in sigma(epsilon) can be modeled with smooth transitions like log(c + exp(c*(epsilon-c0))) added to an elastic backbone.
- Thermomechanical coupling: if temperature effects strengthen only at larger strain (or vice versa), include interaction terms like epsilon*T or multiplicative coupling (hardening term)*(T-dependent factor).
- Parameter identifiability: when both epsilon and T vary, prefer models where T modifies coefficients (E(T), strength(T)) rather than adding many standalone T polynomials to reduce spurious fits.

Expanding: **5.889*epsilon³ + 2.882*T*sin(epsilon) - 806.08*sin(epsilon)**

The GT has three basis function components:
1. **epsilon³** (a power of epsilon)
2. **T*sin(epsilon)** (T times sin of epsilon)
3. **sin(epsilon)** (sin of epsilon alone)

Let me analyze each candidate systematically.

For a candidate to match, it must be able to produce exactly these three terms (and no others that can't be zeroed out).

**Key observations about GT structure:**
- The sin term has argument exactly `epsilon` (not a multiple)
- There's an `epsilon³` term
- T appears linearly multiplied by sin(epsilon)
- No standalone T term, no standalone epsilon term, no constant term (unless absorbed)

Wait, let me re-examine. The GT expanded is: `c0*epsilon³ + c2*T*sin(epsilon) - c2*c3*sin(epsilon)`. So the terms are: epsilon³, T*sin(epsilon), and sin(epsilon).

Let me check each candidate:

### Candidate 1: T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon + c3*exp(T*c4) + c5 + c6*epsilon + c7*sin(c8*epsilon + c9)

Terms: T, T*epsilon, epsilon, exp(T*c4), constant, epsilon, sin(c8*epsilon+c9)

We need T*sin(epsilon), but this has no T*sin term. The T dependence here is only through T, T*epsilon, and exp(T*c4). Setting c4=0 makes exp constant, but then there's no T*sin(epsilon) term. **Cannot match.**

Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 2: T*c0 + T*c1*exp(c2*epsilon) + c3*sin(c4*epsilon+c5) + c6*epsilon + c7 + c8*exp(c2*epsilon)

No T*sin(epsilon) term. T appears as T and T*exp(c2*epsilon). Cannot produce T*sin(epsilon).

Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 3: T*c0 + c1*epsilon + c2*sin(c3*epsilon+c4) + c5 + c6*log(c7*|T|+1)*sin(c8+c9*epsilon)

The T*sin(epsilon) term would need to come from log(c7*|T|+1)*sin(c8+c9*epsilon). But log(c7*|T|+1) ≠ T for any constant. This is not linearly equivalent.

Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 4: T*c0 + T^c1*c2 + c3*sin(c4*epsilon+c5) + c6*epsilon + c7*exp(c8*epsilon) + c9

No T*sin(epsilon) term. T appears only as T*c0 and T^c1. Cannot produce T*sin(epsilon).

Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 5: T*c0 + c1*sin(c2*epsilon+c3) + c4*epsilon + c5*exp(c6*epsilon) + c7 + c8/T^(1/3)

No T*sin(epsilon) term.

Candidate 5 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 6: T*c0 + c1*epsilon + c2 + c3*epsilon*cos(T*c4) + c5*sin(c6*epsilon+c7)

Has epsilon*cos(T*c4) which depends on T inside cosine. Cannot produce T*sin(epsilon).

Candidate 6 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 7: T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon^c3 + c4*epsilon + c5 + c6*epsilon + c7*sin(c8*epsilon+c9)

Terms: T, T*epsilon, epsilon^c3, epsilon, constant, epsilon, sin(c8*epsilon+c9)

We need T*sin(epsilon), but T only appears linearly (T*c0) and as T*epsilon. There's no T*sin term. **Cannot match.**

Candidate 7 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 8: T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon² + c3*epsilon + c4 + c5*epsilon + c6*sin(c7*epsilon+c8)

No T*sin(epsilon). Also epsilon² instead of epsilon³.

Candidate 8 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 9: T*c0 + c1*epsilon + c2*sin(c3*epsilon+c4) + c5*sin(T*c6+c7) + c8

Has sin(T*c6+c7) which is sin of T, not T*sin(epsilon). Cannot produce T*sin(epsilon).

Candidate 9 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 10: T*c0 + c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon⁵ + c3 + c4*log(c5*|T|+1)*sin(c6+c7*epsilon)

Has epsilon⁵ not epsilon³. log(c5*|T|+1) ≠ T.

Candidate 10 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 11: T*c0 + c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon^c3 + c4 + c5*log(c6*|T|+1)*sin(c7+c8*epsilon)

Has epsilon^c3 (good, set c3=3) but log(c6*|T|+1)*sin(...) ≠ T*sin(epsilon).

Candidate 11 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 12: c0*epsilon + c1 + c2*log(c3*|T|+1)*sin(c4+c5*epsilon) + c6*epsilon/(T*c7+c8) + c9/(T*c7+c8)

log term ≠ T. Rational terms in T also don't help.

Candidate 12 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 13: T*c0 + c1*epsilon + c2*sin(c3*epsilon+c4) + c5 + c6*(c7*epsilon+c8)²

Expanding the squared term: c6*c7²*epsilon² + 2*c6*c7*c8*epsilon + c6*c8². This gives epsilon² not epsilon³. No T*sin(epsilon).

Candidate 13 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 20: c0*epsilon + c1 + c2*epsilon^c3 + c4*log(c5*|T|+1)*sin(c6+c7*epsilon)

Has epsilon^c3 (can be epsilon³). But log(c5*|T|+1) ≠ T. Cannot produce T*sin(epsilon).

Candidate 20 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 21: T*c0 + c1*epsilon + c2*sin(c3+c4*epsilon)*|T| + c5 + c6*sin(c3+c4*epsilon)

This is interesting! Let me expand:
- T*c0 + c1*epsilon + c5 + (c2*|T| + c6)*sin(c3+c4*epsilon)

Since T ≥ 0 (temperature), |T| = T. So:
- T*c0 + c1*epsilon + c5 + (c2*T + c6)*sin(c3+c4*epsilon)
- = T*c0 + c1*epsilon + c5 + c2*T*sin(c3+c4*epsilon) + c6*sin(c3+c4*epsilon)

GT = 5.889*epsilon³ + 2.882*T*sin(epsilon) - 806.08*sin(epsilon)

We need:
- c2*T*sin(c3+c4*epsilon) = 2.882*T*sin(epsilon) → c4=1, c3=0 (or c3=2kπ), c2=2.882
- c6*sin(c3+c4*epsilon) = -806.08*sin(epsilon) → c6=-806.08 ✓
- T*c0 = 0 → c0=0
- c1*epsilon = 0 → c1=0
- c5 = 0
- But we need 5.889*epsilon³ and there's no epsilon³ term!

**Cannot produce epsilon³.** 

Candidate 21 verdict: [NO MATCH]
